      class=\"inline-share-btn inline-share-btn-more\"\n         data-share-method=\"facebook\"\n         data-uotrack=\"InlineShareMoreBtn\"><span class=\"inline-share-count inline-share-count-more\"></span><span class=\"inline-share-btn-label inline-share-btn-label-more\">MORE</span></span></div></div><p>\u00a0</p><p>As the sun set on San Bernardino, dozens of people exited a church and lit candles that burned brightly.</p><p class=\"MsoPlainText\">Together, with tears falling down some eyes, they prayed for the souls and families of a special education teacher and her student, who were shot and killed at their elementary school Monday.</p><p>Cedric Anderson shot and killed his wife, Karen Smith, and 8-year-old Jonathan Martinez at North Park Elementary School, then killed himself, according to police.\u00a0</p><div class=\"partner-placement partner-spike\"></div><p>A\u00a09-year-old student was also hit. He was in stable condition at Loma Linda University Medical Center on Tuesday night, officials said.</p><p><span class=\"exclude-from-newsgate\"><strong style=\"margin-right:3px;\">TRAGEDY STRIKES: </strong><a href=\"/story/news/crime_courts/2017/04/10/san-bernardino-elementary-school-shooting/304920001/\">Eight-year-old student dead in San Bernardino school shooting</a></span></p><p>Father Henry Sseriiso, priest at Our Lady of the Assumption a few blocks from the elementary school, urged vigil-goers to pray for victims of violence. But he reminded them that, when violence occurs, hope may follow. </p><p class=\"MsoPlainText\">\"Pray to banish violence and wipe away all tears,\" he told the crowd.</p><div Captions</span></div></div><a class=\"slide-nav prev gallery-prev\" rel=\"prev\">Last Slide</a><a class=\"slide-nav next gallery-next\" rel=\"next\">Next Slide</a></div></div></div><p class=\"MsoPlainText\">Many attendees said they didn't know the victims, but they felt compelled to participate in the service and pray on their behalf.</p><div class=\"partner-outstream\"></div><p class=\"MsoPlainText\">Some people said want to end violence in the city, which in 2016 saw its homicide rate spike. Others said they could relate to the victims.</p><p class=\"MsoPlainText\">Kimberly Phillips' 16-year-old son died seven years ago from an enlarged heart. When she heard a child died in Monday's shooting, she said she felt she had to join the prayer service for its victims.</p><p class=\"MsoPlainText\">\"I know it's a hard thing to deal with,\" said Phillips, 45. \"When I heard it on the news, I just broke down and cried.\"</p><p>San Bernardino has already weathered two violent years.\u00a0In December 2015, county employee Syed Rizwan Farook and his wife, Tashfeen Malik, shot and killed 14 people at a holiday party at the Inland Regional Center in San Bernardino. Investigators determined that the couple had been inspired by foreign extremists and ruled the killings a terrorist act, the deadliest in the U.S. since Sept. 11, 2001 at the time.</p><p><span class=\"exclude-from-newsgate\"><strong style=\"margin-right:3px;\">READ MORE: </strong><a href=\"/story/news/crime_courts/2016/12/01/san-bernardino-shooting/94741128/\">A year later, San Bernardino massacre leaves more questions than answers</a></span></p><p>Then 63 homicides made 2016 the city's deadliest year in more than two decades, according to records compiled by the Los Angeles Times.</p><p class=\"MsoPlainText\">Although she was attending the service to pray for the victims of Monday's shooting, Patricial Kilmer wanted to show the community is united despite a surge in violence. She wore an \"SB Strong\" pin on her shirt.</p><div id=\"module-position-P3eijLgdIa8\" class=\"story-asset image-asset\"><aside itemprop=\"associatedMedia\" itemscope itemtype=\"http://schema.org/ImageObject\" class=\"wide single-photo\"><img itemprop=\"url\" src=\"https://www.gannett-cdn.com/-mm-/e7c866b662bebf1efe4447b572ca408abb4efcc0/c=170-0-2830-2000&amp;r=x408&amp;c=540x405/local/-/media/2017/04/10/PalmSprings/PalmSprings/636274627433272548-SBprayerservice-6.jpg\" alt=\"Suzanne Sullivan cries during a prayer service at Our\" width=\"540\" height=\"405\" data-mycapture-src=\"https://www.gannett-cdn.com/media/2017/04/10/PalmSprings/PalmSprings/636274627433272548-SBprayerservice-6.jpg\"\n                    data-mycapture-sm-src=\"https://www.gannett-cdn.com/-mm-/4044b1e7645488621f157de466cf1a990870caa2/r=500x333/local/-/media/2017/04/10/PalmSprings/PalmSprings/636274627433272548-SBprayerservice-6.jpg\" /><meta itemprop=\"name\" content=\"636274627433272548-SBprayerservice-6.jpg\" /><meta itemprop=\"height\" content=\"405\" /><meta itemprop=\"width\" content=\"540\" /><span class=\"mycapture-btn-wrap\"><span class=\"mycapture-non-priority-horizontal-image mycapture-btn-with-text js-mycapture-btn\">Buy Photo</span></span><p>Suzanne Sullivan cries during a prayer service at Our Lady of the Assumption Church in San Bernardino, Calif., following a school shooting at North Park Elementary School which left one student and a teacher dead, Monday, April 10, 2017.<meta itemprop=\"copyrightHolder\" content=\"Zoe Meyers/The Desert Sun\" />&nbsp;<span class=\"credit\">(Photo: Zoe Meyers/The Desert Sun)</span></p></aside><div class=\"clearfix\"></div></div><p class=\"MsoPlainText\">\"Our residents, they have a lot of pride. They are strong,\" Kilmer said.</p><p class=\"MsoPlainText\">The \"SB Strong\" slogan circulated widely after the 2015 terror attack.</p><p class=\"MsoPlainText\">According to <a href=\"https://everytownresearch.org/school-shootings/#4772\" style=\"background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255);\">Everytown for Gun Safety</a>, a pro-gun control advocacy group, the shooting at North Park Elementary was the fourth intentional shooting on a K-12 campus in the U.S. in 2017 and the first deadly shooting.</p><p class=\"MsoPlainText\">The group counted two other shootings at schools, but in both cases, guns had been accidentally discharged.</p><p><span class=\"exclude-from-newsgate\"><strong style=\"margin-right:3px;\">READ MORE: </strong><a href=\"/story/news/local/rancho-mirage/2016/11/30/san-bernardino-mass-shootings-one-year-later-police-lt-michael-madden/94294804/\">San Bernardino terror attack first responders relive 'horrific scene'</a></span></p><p class=\"MsoPlainText\">As people prayed in San Bernardino on Tuesday, volunteers from area nonprofit organizations handed out flyers for an April 27 prayer walk to end gun violence. Michelle Sabino, who represented HOPE Culture, which helps children, said efforts to curb violence should go beyond prayer.</p><div id=\"module-position-P3eijLh03-c\" class=\"story-asset image-asset\"><aside itemprop=\"associatedMedia\" itemscope itemtype=\"http://schema.org/ImageObject\" class=\"wide single-photo\"><img itemprop=\"url\" src=\"https://www.gannett-cdn.com/-mm-/e7c866b662bebf1efe4447b572ca408abb4efcc0/c=170-0-2830-2000&amp;r=x408&amp;c=540x405/local/-/media/2017/04/10/PalmSprings/PalmSprings/636274627435300561-SBprayerservice-2.jpg\" alt=\"People gather for a prayer service at Our Lady of the\" width=\"540\" height=\"405\" data-mycapture-src=\"https://www.gannett-cdn.com/media/2017/04/10/PalmSprings/PalmSprings/636274627435300561-SBprayerservice-2.jpg\"\n                    data-mycapture-sm-src=\"https://www.gannett-cdn.com/-mm-/4044b1e7645488621f157de466cf1a990870caa2/r=500x333/local/-/media/2017/04/10/PalmSprings/PalmSprings/636274627435300561-SBprayerservice-2.jpg\" /><meta itemprop=\"name\" content=\"636274627435300561-SBprayerservice-2.jpg\" /><meta itemprop=\"height\" content=\"405\" /><meta itemprop=\"width\" content=\"540\" /><span class=\"mycapture-btn-wrap\"><span class=\"mycapture-non-priority-horizontal-image mycapture-btn-with-text js-mycapture-btn\">Buy Photo</span></span><p>People gather for a prayer service at Our Lady class=\"MsoPlainText\">\"If you're concerned with this city, stand with this city,\" she said.</p><p class=\"MsoPlainText\">Sabino said a big step would be explaining what types of organizations exist to help residents, particularly children.</p><p class=\"MsoPlainText\">\"It's having people understand our youth are dealing with situations they shouldn't have to deal with,\" she said.</p><div (April 10) AP 6 of 6 Last VideoNext Video After learning of the shooting, a mother rushes to the San Bernardino school where it happened\n\n2 adults, 1 child dead from elementary school shooting\n\nAfter picking up her child, a parent reacts to San Bernardino elementary school shooting\n\nShots fired at San Bernardino elementary school\n\nParents await kids after Calif. school shooting\n\nMom hopeful for reunion after school shooting\n\nBuy Photo A boy prays on his father's shoulder during a prayer service at Our Lady of the Assumption Church in San Bernardino, Calif. The service followed a school shooting at North Park Elementary School which left one student and a teacher dead, Monday, April 10, 2017. (Photo: Zoe Meyers/The Desert Sun)Buy Photo\n\nAs the sun set on San Bernardino, dozens of people exited a church and lit candles that burned brightly.\n\nTogether, with tears falling down some eyes, they prayed for the souls and families of a special education teacher and her student, who were shot and killed at their elementary school Monday.\n\nCedric Anderson shot and killed his wife, Karen Smith, and 8-year-old Jonathan Martinez at North Park Elementary School, then killed himself, according to police.\n\nA 9-year-old student was also hit. He was in stable condition at Loma Linda University Medical Center on Tuesday night, officials said.\n\nTRAGEDY STRIKES: Eight-year-old student dead in San Bernardino school shooting\n\nFather Henry Sseriiso, priest at Our Lady of the Assumption a few blocks from the elementary school, urged vigil-goers to pray for victims of violence. But he reminded them that, when violence occurs, hope may follow.\n\n\"Pray to banish violence and wipe away all tears,\" he told the crowd.\n\nMany attendees said they didn't know the victims, but they felt compelled to participate in the service and pray on their behalf.\n\nSome people said want to end violence in the city, which in 2016 saw its homicide rate spike. Others said they could relate to the victims.\n\nKimberly Phillips' 16-year-old son died seven years ago from an enlarged heart. When she heard a child died in Monday's shooting, she said she felt she had to join the prayer service for its victims.\n\n\"I know it's a hard thing to deal with,\" said Phillips, 45. \"When I heard it on the news, I just broke down and cried.\"\n\nSan Bernardino has already weathered two violent years. In December 2015, county employee Syed Rizwan Farook and his wife, Tashfeen Malik, shot and killed 14 people at a holiday party at the Inland Regional Center in San Bernardino. Investigators determined that the couple had been inspired by foreign extremists and ruled the killings a terrorist act, the deadliest in the U.S. since Sept. 11, 2001 at the time.\n\nREAD MORE: A year later, San Bernardino massacre leaves more questions than answers\n\nThen 63 homicides made 2016 the city's deadliest year in more than two decades, according to records compiled by the Los Angeles Times.\n\nAlthough she was attending the service to pray for the victims of Monday's shooting, Patricial Kilmer wanted to show the community is united despite a surge in violence. She wore an \"SB Strong\" pin on her shirt.\n\nBuy Photo Suzanne Sullivan cries during a prayer service at Our Lady of the Assumption Church in San Bernardino, Calif., following a school shooting at North Park Elementary School which left one student and a teacher dead, Monday, April 10, 2017. (Photo: Zoe Meyers/The Desert Sun)\n\n\"Our residents, they have a lot of pride. They are strong,\" Kilmer said.\n\nThe \"SB Strong\" slogan circulated widely after the 2015 terror attack.\n\nAccording to Everytown for Gun Safety, a pro-gun control advocacy group, the shooting at North Park Elementary was the fourth intentional shooting on a K-12 campus in the U.S. in 2017 and the first deadly shooting.\n\nThe group counted two other shootings at schools, but in both cases, guns had been accidentally discharged.\n\nREAD MORE: San Bernardino terror attack first responders relive 'horrific scene'\n\nAs people prayed in San Bernardino on Tuesday, volunteers from area nonprofit organizations handed out flyers for an April 27 prayer walk to end gun violence. Michelle Sabino, who represented HOPE Culture, which helps children, said efforts to curb violence should go beyond prayer.\n\nBuy Photo People gather for a prayer service at Our Lady of the Assumption Church in San Bernardino, Calif., following a school shooting at North Park Elementary School which left one student and a teacher dead, Monday, April 10, 2017. (Photo: Zoe Meyers/The Desert Sun)\n\n\"If you're concerned with this city, stand with this city,\" she said.\n\nSabino said a big step would be explaining what types of organizations exist to help residents, particularly children.\n\n\"It's having people understand our youth are dealing with situations they shouldn't have to deal with,\" she said.\n\nRead or Share this story:
